class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_England" title="Privy Council of England">Privy Council of England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_Scotland" title="Privy Council of Scotland">Privy Council of Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_law" title="English law">English law</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scots_law" title="Scots law">Scots law</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Privy Council">Privy Council</a> of the United Kingdom was preceded by the Privy Council of Scotland and the Privy Council of England. The key events in the formation of the modern Privy Council are given below:\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Saxon England">Anglo-Saxon England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Witenagemot" title="Witenagemot">Witenagemot</a> was an early equivalent to the <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_England" title="Privy Council of England">Privy Council of England</a>. During the reigns of the <a href="/wiki/Norman_Conquest" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman Conquest">Norman monarchs</a>, the <a href="/wiki/English_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="English Crown">English Crown</a> was advised by a <a href="/wiki/Royal_court" title="Royal court">royal court</a> or <i><a href="/wiki/Curia_regis" title="Curia regis">curia regis</a></i>, which consisted of <a href="/wiki/Magnate" title="Magnate">magnates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastic" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecclesiastic">ecclesiastics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Law_Officers_of_the_Crown" title="Law Officers of the Crown">high officials</a>. The body originally concerned itself with advising the sovereign on legislation, administration and justice.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Later, different bodies assuming distinct functions evolved from the court. The courts of law took over the business of dispensing <a href="/wiki/Justice" title="Justice">justice</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_England" title="Parliament of England">Parliament</a> became the supreme legislature of the kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Nevertheless, the Council retained the power to hear legal disputes, either in the first instance or on appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, laws made by the sovereign on the advice of the Council, rather than on the advice of Parliament, were accepted as valid.<sup id="cite_ref-gay-p2_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p2-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Powerful sovereigns often used the body to circumvent the Courts and Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-gay-p2_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p2-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> For example, a committee of the Council\xe2\x80\x94which later became the <a href="/wiki/Star_Chamber" title="Star Chamber">Court of the Star Chamber</a>\xe2\x80\x94was during the 15th century permitted to inflict any punishment except death, without being bound by normal <a href="/wiki/Trial" title="Trial">court procedure</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> During <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII\'s</a> reign, the sovereign, on the advice of the Council, was allowed to enact laws by mere proclamation. The legislative pre-eminence of Parliament was not restored until after Henry VIII\'s death.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Though the royal Council retained legislative and judicial responsibilities, it became a primarily administrative body.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The Council consisted of forty members in 1553,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> but the sovereign relied on a smaller committee, which later evolved into the modern <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Cabinet of the United Kingdom">Cabinet</a>.\n</p><p>By the end of the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>, the monarchy, House of Lords, and Privy Council had been abolished. The remaining <a href="/wiki/Chambers_of_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Chambers of parliament">parliamentary chamber</a>, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_England" title="House of Commons of England">House of Commons</a>, instituted a <a href="/wiki/English_Council_of_State" title="English Council of State">Council of State</a> to execute laws and to direct administrative policy. The forty-one members of the Council were elected by the House of Commons; the body was headed by <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> military dictator of the nation. In 1653, however, Cromwell became <a href="/wiki/Lord_Protector" title="Lord Protector">Lord Protector</a>, and the Council was reduced to between thirteen and twenty-one members, all elected by the Commons. In 1657, the Commons granted Cromwell even greater powers, some of which were reminiscent of those enjoyed by monarchs. The Council became known as the <a href="/wiki/Protector%27s_Privy_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Protector&#39;s Privy Council">Protector\'s Privy Council</a>; its members were appointed by the Lord Protector, subject to Parliament\'s approval.<sup id="cite_ref-plant_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plant-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1659, shortly before the <a href="/wiki/English_Restoration" class="mw-redirect" title="English Restoration">restoration of the monarchy</a>, the Protector\'s Council was abolished.<sup id="cite_ref-plant_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plant-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II</a> restored the Royal Privy Council, but he, like previous <a href="/wiki/House_of_Stuart" title="House of Stuart">Stuart</a> monarchs, chose to rely on a small group of advisers.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Under <a href="/wiki/George_I_of_Great_Britain" title="George I of Great Britain">George I</a> even more power transferred to this committee. It now began to meet in the absence of the sovereign, communicating its decisions to him after the fact.\n</p><p>Thus, the British Privy Council, as a whole, ceased to be a body of important confidential advisers to the sovereign; the role passed to a committee of the Council, now known as the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Cabinet of the United Kingdom">Cabinet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin_of_the_term">Origin of the term</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origin of the term">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a></i>, the definition of the word <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/privy" class="extiw" title="wikt:privy">privy</a></i> in <i>Privy Council</i> is obsolete meaning "of or pertaining exclusively to a particular person or persons, one\'s own";<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> hence the Council is personal to the sovereign. It is closely related to the word <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/private" class="extiw" title="wikt:private">private</a></i>, and derives from the <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> word <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/priv%C3%A9" class="extiw" title="wikt:priv\xc3\xa9">priv\xc3\xa9</a></i>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomas_Rowlandson_-_The_Privy_Council_of_a_King_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Thomas_Rowlandson_-_The_Privy_Council_of_a_King_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/300px-Thomas_Rowlandson_-_The_Privy_Council_of_a_King_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" width="300" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Thomas_Rowlandson_-_The_Privy_Council_of_a_King_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/450px-Thomas_Rowlandson_-_The_Privy_Council_of_a_King_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Thomas_Rowlandson_-_The_Privy_Council_of_a_King_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/600px-Thomas_Rowlandson_-_The_Privy_Council_of_a_King_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4468" data-file-height="3183" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomas_Rowlandson_-_The_Privy_Council_of_a_King_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Privy Council of a King</i> by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Rowlandson" title="Thomas Rowlandson">Thomas Rowlandson</a>. 1815</div></div></div>\n<p>The sovereign, when acting on the Council\'s advice, is known as the <i><a href="/wiki/King-in-Council" title="King-in-Council">King-in-Council</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Queen-in-Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen-in-Council">Queen-in-Council</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The members of the Council are collectively known as <i>The Lords of Her Majesty\'s Most Honourable Privy Council</i><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> (sometimes <i>The Lords and others of&#160;...</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Chief_officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief officer">chief officer</a> of the body is the <a href="/wiki/Lord_President_of_the_Council" title="Lord President of the Council">Lord President of the Council</a>, who is the fourth highest <a href="/wiki/Great_Officer_of_State" title="Great Officer of State">Great Officer of State</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Cabinet of the United Kingdom">Cabinet member</a> and normally, either the Leader of the House of Lords or of the House of Commons.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Another important official is the <a href="/wiki/Clerk_of_the_Privy_Council_(United_Kingdom)" title="Clerk of the Privy Council (United Kingdom)">Clerk</a>, whose signature is appended to all orders made in the Council.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Both <i>Privy Counsellor</i> and <i>Privy Councillor</i> may be correctly used to refer to a member of the Council. The former, however, is preferred by the <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_Office_(United_Kingdom)" title="Privy Council Office (United Kingdom)">Privy Council Office</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-business-faq_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-business-faq-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> emphasising English usage of the term <i>Counsellor</i> as "one who gives <a href="/wiki/Counsel" title="Counsel">counsel</a>", as opposed to "one who is a member of a council". A Privy Counsellor is traditionally said to be "<i>sworn of</i>" the Council after being received by the sovereign.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The sovereign may appoint anyone a Privy Counsellor,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> but in practice appointments are made only on the advice of <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Her Majesty&#39;s Government">Her Majesty\'s Government</a>. The majority of appointees are senior politicians, including Ministers of the Crown, the few most senior figures of <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Most_Loyal_Opposition_(United_Kingdom)" title="Her Majesty&#39;s Most Loyal Opposition (United Kingdom)">Loyal Opposition</a>, the Parliamentary leader of the third-largest party, a couple of the most senior figures in the devolved British governments and senior politicians from Commonwealth countries. Besides these, the Council includes a very few members of the <a href="/wiki/British_Royal_Family" class="mw-redirect" title="British Royal Family">Royal Family</a> (usually the <a href="/wiki/Prince_consort" title="Prince consort">consort</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heir_apparent" title="Heir apparent">heir apparent</a> only), a few dozen judges from British and Commonwealth countries, a few clergy and a small number of senior civil servants.\n</p><p>There is no statutory limit to its membership:<sup id="cite_ref-gay-p3_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p3-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> at January 2012, there were about 600 members;<sup id="cite_ref-pc-members_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-members-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> they had risen in number to over 650 by June 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However, the members have no automatic right to attend all Privy Council meetings, and only some are summoned regularly to meetings (in practice at the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister</a>\'s discretion).\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a>\'s three senior <a href="/wiki/Bishop" title="Bishop">bishops</a>\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishop of Canterbury</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_York" title="Archbishop of York">Archbishop of York</a><sup id="cite_ref-gay-p3_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p3-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_London" title="Bishop of London">Bishop of London</a><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94become Privy Counsellors upon appointment. Senior members of the Royal Family may also be appointed, but this is confined to the current consort and heir apparent and consort.<sup id="cite_ref-gay-p3_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p3-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Philip">Prince Philip</a> is at present the most senior member by length of service,<sup id="cite_ref-pc-members_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-members-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and he is the only current Privy Counsellor not appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">reigning monarch</a>, having been sworn of the Council by <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">her father</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Private_Secretary_to_the_Sovereign" title="Private Secretary to the Sovereign">Private Secretary to the Sovereign</a> is always appointed a Privy Counsellor,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> as are the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chamberlain" title="Lord Chamberlain">Lord Chamberlain</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_House_of_Commons_(United_Kingdom)" title="Speaker of the House of Commons (United Kingdom)">Speaker of the House of Commons</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Speaker" title="Lord Speaker">Lord Speaker</a>. <a href="/wiki/Justice_of_the_Supreme_Court_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Justice of the Supreme Court of the United Kingdom">Justices</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Supreme Court of the United Kingdom">Supreme Court of the United Kingdom</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> judges of the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal_of_England_and_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="Court of Appeal of England and Wales">Court of Appeal of England and Wales</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> senior judges of the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Session" title="Court of Session">Inner House of the Court of Session</a> (Scotland\'s highest law court)<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chief_Justice_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Lord Chief Justice of Northern Ireland">Lord Chief Justice of Northern Ireland</a><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> also join the Privy Council <i>ex officio</i>.\n</p><p>The balance of Privy Counsellors is largely made up of <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">politicians</a>. The Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Cabinet of the United Kingdom">Cabinet</a> <a href="/wiki/Minister_(government)" title="Minister (government)">ministers</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Leader of the Opposition (UK)">Leader of HM Opposition</a> are traditionally sworn of the Privy Council upon appointment.<sup id="cite_ref-gay-p3_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p3-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Leaders of major <a href="/wiki/Political_parties_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Political parties in the United Kingdom">parties</a> in the House of Commons, <a href="/wiki/First_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="First Minister">First Ministers</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">devolved assemblies</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> some senior <a href="/wiki/Minister_(government)" title="Minister (government)">Ministers</a> outside Cabinet, and on occasion other respected senior parliamentarians are appointed Privy Counsellors.\n</p><p>Because Privy Counsellors are bound by <a href="/wiki/Oath" title="Oath">oath</a> to keep matters discussed at Council meetings secret, the appointment of the Leaders of Opposition Parties as Privy Counsellors allows the Government to share confidential information with them "on Privy Council terms".<sup id="cite_ref-gay-p3_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p3-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> This usually only happens in special circumstances, such as in matters of <a href="/wiki/National_security" title="National security">national security</a>. For example, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> met <a href="/wiki/Iain_Duncan_Smith" title="Iain Duncan Smith">Iain Duncan Smith</a> (then Leader of HM Opposition) and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Kennedy" title="Charles Kennedy">Charles Kennedy</a> (then <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Liberal_Democrats" title="Leader of the Liberal Democrats">Leader of the Liberal Democrats</a>) "on Privy Council terms" to discuss the <a href="/wiki/September_Dossier" title="September Dossier">evidence for Iraq\'s weapons of mass destruction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-so-what_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-so-what-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although the Privy Council is primarily a British institution, officials from some other <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a> are also appointed.<sup id="cite_ref-gay-p3_22-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p3-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> By 2000, the most notable instance was New Zealand, whose <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_New_Zealand" title="Prime Minister of New Zealand">Prime Minister</a>, senior politicians, Chief Justice and Court of Appeal Justices were traditionally appointed Privy Counsellors.<sup id="cite_ref-nz-pc_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nz-pc-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> However, appointments of New Zealand members have since been discontinued. The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_New_Zealand" title="Prime Minister of New Zealand">Prime Minister</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_New_Zealand_House_of_Representatives" title="Speaker of the New Zealand House of Representatives">Speaker</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_New_Zealand" title="Governor-General of New Zealand">Governor-General</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_New_Zealand" title="Chief Justice of New Zealand">Chief Justice of New Zealand</a> are still accorded the <a href="/wiki/Style_(manner_of_address)" title="Style (manner of address)">style</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Right_Honourable" class="mw-redirect" title="Right Honourable">Right Honourable</a></i>, but without membership of the Council.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Until the late 20th century, the Prime Ministers and Chief Justices of Canada and Australia were also appointed Privy Counsellors.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Canada also has its own Privy Council, the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Privy_Council_for_Canada" title="Queen&#39;s Privy Council for Canada">Queen\'s Privy Council for Canada</a> (<i>see</i> <a href="#Other_councils">below</a>). Prime Ministers of some other Commonwealth countries that retain the Queen as their sovereign continue to be sworn of the Council.<sup id="cite_ref-gay-p3_22-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p3-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Privy_Council_oath_and_initiation_rite">Privy Council oath and initiation rite</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Privy Council oath and initiation rite">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Viviana_examined_by_the_Earl_of_Salisbury,_and_the_Privy_Council_in_the_Star_Chamber.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Viviana_examined_by_the_Earl_of_Salisbury%2C_and_the_Privy_Council_in_the_Star_Chamber.png/250px-Viviana_examined_by_the_Earl_of_Salisbury%2C_and_the_Privy_Council_in_the_Star_Chamber.png" width="250" height="309" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Viviana_examined_by_the_Earl_of_Salisbury%2C_and_the_Privy_Council_in_the_Star_Chamber.png/375px-Viviana_examined_by_the_Earl_of_Salisbury%2C_and_the_Privy_Council_in_the_Star_Chamber.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a7/Viviana_examined_by_the_Earl_of_Salisbury%2C_and_the_Privy_Council_in_the_Star_Chamber.png 2x" data-file-width="386" data-file-height="477" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Viviana_examined_by_the_Earl_of_Salisbury,_and_the_Privy_Council_in_the_Star_Chamber.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Viviana Radcliffe examined by the Earl of Salisbury, and the Privy Council in the Star Chamber. Illustration by George Cruikshank from William Harrison Ainsworth\'s novel <i>Guy Fawkes</i>.</div></div></div>\n<p>It was formerly regarded by the Privy Council as criminal, and possibly <a href="/wiki/Treason" title="Treason">treasonous</a>, to disclose the <a href="/wiki/Oath" title="Oath">oath</a> administered to Privy Counsellors as they take office.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> However, the oath was officially made public by the <a href="/wiki/Blair_ministry" title="Blair ministry">Blair Government</a> in a written parliamentary answer in 1998, as follows.<sup id="cite_ref-pcoath_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcoath-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> It had also been read out in full in the House of Lords during debate by <a href="/wiki/James_Hope,_1st_Baron_Rankeillour" title="James Hope, 1st Baron Rankeillour">Lord Rankeillour</a> on 21 December 1932.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>You do swear by Almighty God to be a true and faithful Servant unto the Queen\'s Majesty, as one of Her Majesty\'s Privy Council. You will not know or understand of any manner of thing to be attempted, done, or spoken against Her Majesty\'s Person, Honour, Crown, or Dignity Royal, but you will let and withstand the same to the uttermost of your Power, and either cause it to be revealed to Her Majesty Herself, or to such of Her Privy Council as shall advertise Her Majesty of the same. You will, in all things to be moved, treated, and debated in Council, faithfully and truly declare your Mind and Opinion, according to your Heart and Conscience; and will keep secret all Matters committed and revealed unto you, or that shall be treated of secretly in Council. And if any of the said Treaties or Counsels shall touch any of the Counsellors, you will not reveal it unto him, but will keep the same until such time as, by the Consent of Her Majesty, or of the Council, Publication shall be made thereof. You will to your uttermost bear Faith and Allegiance unto the Queen\'s Majesty; and will assist and defend all Jurisdictions, Pre-eminences, and Authorities, granted to Her Majesty, and annexed to the Crown by Acts of Parliament, or otherwise, against all Foreign Princes, Persons, Prelates, States, or Potentates. And generally in all things you will do as a faithful and true Servant ought to do to Her Majesty. So help you God.<sup id="cite_ref-pcoath_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcoath-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>A form of this oath dates back to at least 1570.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Privy_counsellor" class="mw-redirect" title="Privy counsellor">Privy counsellors</a> can choose to <a href="/wiki/Affirmation_in_law" title="Affirmation in law">affirm</a> their allegiance in similar terms, should they prefer not to take a religious oath.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> At the induction ceremony, the order of precedence places <a href="/wiki/Anglicans" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglicans">Anglicans</a> (being those of the <a href="/wiki/Established_church" class="mw-redirect" title="Established church">established church</a>) before others.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-20150918_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-20150918-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The initiation ceremony for newly appointed privy counsellors is held in private, and typically requires kneeling on a stool before the sovereign and then <a href="/wiki/Kissing_hands" title="Kissing hands">kissing hands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rite_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rite-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> According to <i>The Royal Encyclopaedia</i>: "The new privy counsellor or minister will extend his or her right hand, palm upwards, and, taking the Queen\'s hand lightly, will kiss it with no more than a touch of the lips."<sup id="cite_ref-Rite_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rite-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The ceremony has caused difficulties for privy counsellors who advocate <a href="/wiki/Republicanism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Republicanism in the United Kingdom">republicanism</a>; <a href="/wiki/Tony_Benn" title="Tony Benn">Tony Benn</a> said in his diaries that he kissed his own thumb, rather than the Queen\'s hand, while <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Corbyn" title="Jeremy Corbyn">Jeremy Corbyn</a> reportedly did not kneel.<sup id="cite_ref-Rite_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rite-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Not all members of the privy council go through the initiation ceremony; appointments are frequently made by an <a href="/wiki/Order_in_Council" title="Order in Council">Order in Council</a>, although it is "rare for a party leader to use such a course."<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Term_of_office">Term of office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Term of office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Membership is conferred for life. Formerly, the death of a monarch ("<a href="/wiki/Demise_of_the_Crown" title="Demise of the Crown">demise of the Crown</a>") brought an immediate dissolution of the Council, as all <a href="/wiki/Royal_prerogative_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal prerogative in the United Kingdom">Crown appointments</a> automatically lapsed.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> By the 18th century, it was enacted that the Council would not be dissolved until up to six months after the demise of the Crown.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> By convention, however, the sovereign would reappoint all members of the Council after its dissolution.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In practice, therefore, membership continued without a break.<sup id="cite_ref-gay-p3_22-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p3-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In 1901, the <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Law of the United Kingdom">law</a> was changed to ensure that Crown Appointments became wholly unaffected by any succession of monarch.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The sovereign, however, may remove an individual from the Privy Council. Former MP <a href="/wiki/Elliot_Morley" title="Elliot Morley">Elliot Morley</a> was expelled on 8 June 2011, following his <a href="/wiki/Conviction" title="Conviction">conviction</a> on charges of false accounting in connection with the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_parliamentary_expenses_scandal" title="United Kingdom parliamentary expenses scandal">British parliamentary expenses scandal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Morley_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morley-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Before this, the last individual to be expelled from the Council against his will was <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Speyer" title="Edgar Speyer">Sir Edgar Speyer, <small>Bt.</small></a>, who was removed on 13 December 1921<sup id="cite_ref-resignb_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-resignb-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Speyer_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Speyer-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> for collaborating with the enemy <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-beeb_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beeb-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Individuals can choose to resign, sometimes to avoid expulsion. Three members voluntarily left the Privy Council in the 20th century: <a href="/wiki/John_Profumo" title="John Profumo">John Profumo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-beeb_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beeb-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> who resigned on 26 June 1963;<sup id="cite_ref-resigna_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-resigna-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Profumo_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Profumo-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Stonehouse" title="John Stonehouse">John Stonehouse</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-beeb_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beeb-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> who resigned on 17 August 1976<sup id="cite_ref-resigna_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-resigna-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stonehouse_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stonehouse-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Aitken" title="Jonathan Aitken">Jonathan Aitken</a>, who resigned on 25 June 1997<sup id="cite_ref-resign_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-resign-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> following allegations of <a href="/wiki/Perjury" title="Perjury">perjury</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-beeb_55-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beeb-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Aitken_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aitken-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>So far, three Privy Counsellors have resigned in the 21st century, coincidentally all in the same year. On 4 February 2013, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Huhne" title="Chris Huhne">Chris Huhne</a> announced that he would voluntarily leave the Privy Council after pleading guilty to <a href="/wiki/Perverting_the_course_of_justice" title="Perverting the course of justice">perverting the course of justice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Prescott" title="John Prescott">Lord Prescott</a> stood down on 6 July 2013, in protest against delays in the introduction of press regulation, expecting others to follow.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Denis_MacShane" title="Denis MacShane">Denis MacShane</a> resigned on 9 October 2013, before a High Court hearing at which he pleaded guilty of false accounting and was subsequently imprisoned.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meetings">Meetings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Meetings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Privy_Council_(Wilke).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Victoria_Privy_Council_%28Wilke%29.jpg/300px-Victoria_Privy_Council_%28Wilke%29.jpg" width="300" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Victoria_Privy_Council_%28Wilke%29.jpg/450px-Victoria_Privy_Council_%28Wilke%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Victoria_Privy_Council_%28Wilke%29.jpg/600px-Victoria_Privy_Council_%28Wilke%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="754" data-file-height="478" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Privy_Council_(Wilke).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> convened her first <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Privy Council">Privy Council</a> on the day of her <a href="/wiki/Accession_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Accession Day">accession</a> in 1837.</div></div></div>\n<p>Meetings of the Privy Council are normally held once each month wherever the sovereign may be in residence at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-royal.gov-pc_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-royal.gov-pc-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Quorum" title="Quorum">quorum</a>, according to the Privy Council Office, is three,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> though some statutes provide for other quorums (for example, section 35 of the <a href="/wiki/General_Optical_Council" title="General Optical Council">Opticians Act 1989</a><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> provides for a lower quorum of two).\n</p><p>The sovereign attends the meeting, though his or her place may be taken by two or more <a href="/wiki/Counsellors_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Counsellors of State">Counsellors of State</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gay-p4_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p4-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-counsellors-of-state_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-counsellors-of-state-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Under the Regency Acts 1937 to 1953,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Counsellor_of_State" title="Counsellor of State">Counsellors of State</a> may be chosen from among the sovereign\'s spouse and the four individuals next in the line of succession who are over 21 years of age (18 for the <a href="/wiki/Succession_to_the_British_throne" title="Succession to the British throne">heir to the throne</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-counsellors-of-state_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-counsellors-of-state-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Customarily the sovereign remains standing at meetings of the Privy Council, so that no other members may sit down,<sup id="cite_ref-business-faq_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-business-faq-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> thereby keeping meetings short. The <a href="/wiki/Lord_President_of_the_Council" title="Lord President of the Council">Lord President</a> reads out a list of Orders to be made, and the sovereign merely says "Approved".<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Few Privy Counsellors are required to attend regularly. The settled practice is that day-to-day meetings of the Council are attended by four Privy Counsellors, usually the relevant Minister to the matters pertaining.<sup id="cite_ref-gay-p4_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p4-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The Cabinet Minister holding the office of <a href="/wiki/Lord_President_of_the_Council" title="Lord President of the Council">Lord President of the Council</a>, currently the <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Leadsom" title="Andrea Leadsom">Rt Hon. Andrea Leadsom</a> <span class="noexcerpt" style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of the British House of Commons">MP</a></span>,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> invariably presides.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Under Britain\'s modern conventions of <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary government">parliamentary government</a> and <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>, every order made in Council is drafted by a <a href="/wiki/Civil_Service_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Service (United Kingdom)">Government Department</a> and has already been approved by the <a href="/wiki/Minister_(government)" title="Minister (government)">Minister</a> responsible\xe2\x80\x94thus actions taken by the <a href="/wiki/Queen-in-Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen-in-Council">Queen-in-Council</a> are formalities required for validation of each measure.<sup id="cite_ref-gay-p4_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p4-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Full meetings of the Privy Council are held only when the reigning sovereign announces his or her own engagement (which last happened on 23 November 1839,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> in the reign of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>); or when there is a <a href="/wiki/Demise_of_the_Crown" title="Demise of the Crown">demise of the Crown</a>, either by the death or abdication of the <a href="/wiki/Monarch" title="Monarch">monarch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-so-what_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-so-what-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> A full meeting of the Privy Council was also held on 6 February 1811, when <a href="/wiki/George_IV_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George IV of the United Kingdom">George, Prince of Wales</a> was sworn in as <a href="/wiki/Prince_Regent" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Regent">Prince Regent</a> by <a href="/wiki/Regency_Acts" title="Regency Acts">Act of Parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Regency_Acts" title="Regency Acts">current statutes regulating the establishment of a regency</a> in the case of minority or incapacity of the sovereign also require any <a href="/wiki/Prince_Regent" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Regent">regents</a> to swear their oaths before the Privy Council.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the case of a demise of the Crown, the Privy Council\xe2\x80\x94together with the <a href="/wiki/Lords_Spiritual" title="Lords Spiritual">Lords Spiritual</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lords_Temporal" title="Lords Temporal">Lords Temporal</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor_of_the_City_of_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayor of the City of London">Lord Mayor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Aldermen" title="Court of Aldermen">Aldermen</a> of the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City of London</a> as well as representatives of <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a>\xe2\x80\x94makes a proclamation declaring the accession of the new sovereign and receives an oath from the new monarch relating to the security of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a>, as required by law. It is also customary for the new sovereign to make an <a href="/wiki/Allocution" title="Allocution">allocution</a> to the Privy Council on that occasion, and this Sovereign\'s Speech is formally published in <i>The <a href="/wiki/London_Gazette" class="mw-redirect" title="London Gazette">London Gazette</a></i>. Any such Special Assembly of the Privy Council, convened to proclaim the accession of a new sovereign and witness the monarch\'s statutory oath, is known as an <a href="/wiki/Accession_Council" title="Accession Council">Accession Council</a>. The last such meetings were held on 6 and 8 February 1952: as <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> was abroad when the last <a href="/wiki/Demise_of_the_Crown" title="Demise of the Crown">demise of the Crown</a> took place, the Accession Council met twice, once to proclaim the sovereign (meeting of 6 February 1952), and then again after the new queen had returned to Britain, to receive from her the oath required by statute (meeting of 8 February 1952).<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Functions">Functions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Functions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The sovereign exercises executive authority by making <a href="/wiki/Order_in_Council" title="Order in Council">Orders in Council</a> upon the advice of the Privy Council. Orders-in-Council, which are drafted by the <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Her Majesty&#39;s Government">government</a> rather than by the sovereign, are secondary legislation and are used to make government regulations and to make government appointments. Furthermore, Orders-in-Council are used to grant <a href="/wiki/Royal_Assent" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Assent">Royal Assent</a> for <a href="/wiki/Measures_of_the_National_Assembly_for_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="Measures of the National Assembly for Wales">Measures of the National Assembly for Wales</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">laws</a> passed by the <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislatures</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Crown" title="The Crown">British</a> <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependency" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown dependency">Crown dependencies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factsheet-l7_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factsheet-l7-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Distinct from Orders-in-Council are <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Council" title="Order of Council">Orders of Council</a>: the former are issued by the sovereign upon the advice of the Privy Council, whereas the latter are made by members of the Privy Council without requiring the sovereign\'s approval. They are issued under the specific authority of <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Parliament" title="Act of Parliament">Acts of Parliament</a>, and most commonly are used for the regulation of <a href="/wiki/Institute" title="Institute">public institutions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factsheet-l7_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factsheet-l7-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The sovereign also grants <a href="/wiki/Royal_Charter" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Charter">Royal Charters</a> on the advice of the Privy Council. Charters bestow special status to <a href="/wiki/Incorporation_(association)" class="mw-redirect" title="Incorporation (association)">incorporated bodies</a>; they are used to grant <a href="/wiki/List_of_British_professional_bodies#Chartered" class="mw-redirect" title="List of British professional bodies">"chartered"</a> status to certain <a href="/wiki/Professional_association" title="Professional association">professional</a>, educational or charitable bodies, and sometimes also <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borough" title="Borough">borough</a> status to towns.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The Privy Council therefore deals with a wide range of matters, which also includes university and <a href="/wiki/Livery_company" title="Livery company">livery company</a> statutes,<sup id="cite_ref-gay-p5_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p5-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> the grant of academic degree-awarding powers (e.g. taught degree awarding powers (TDAP))<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Churchyard" title="Churchyard">churchyards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> coinage and dates of <a href="/wiki/Bank_holiday" title="Bank holiday">bank holidays</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-royal.gov-pc_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-royal.gov-pc-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Committees">Committees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Committees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council_-_Court_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council_-_Court_3.jpg/300px-Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council_-_Court_3.jpg" width="300" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council_-_Court_3.jpg/450px-Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council_-_Court_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council_-_Court_3.jpg/600px-Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council_-_Court_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="958" data-file-height="538" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council_-_Court_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Judicial Committee of the Privy Council.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Privy Council comprises a number of Standing Committees:<sup id="cite_ref-whatdotheyknow_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatdotheyknow-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Standing_Council_of_the_Baronetage" title="Standing Council of the Baronetage">Baronetage Committee</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Cabinet of the United Kingdom">Cabinet of the United Kingdom</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Jersey" title="Politics of Jersey">Committee for the Affairs of Jersey and Guernsey</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Letters_patent" title="Letters patent">Committee for the Purposes of the Crown Office Act 1877</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council" title="Judicial Committee of the Privy Council">Judicial Committee of the Privy Council</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ancient_universities_of_Scotland" title="Ancient universities of Scotland">Scottish Universities Committee</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Universities_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Universities in the United Kingdom">Universities Committee</a></li></ul>\n<p>The Baronetage Committee was established by a 1910 <a href="/wiki/Order_in_Council" title="Order in Council">Order in Council</a>, during <a href="/wiki/Edward_VII" title="Edward VII">Edward VII</a>\'s reign, to scrutinise all succession claims (and thus reject doubtful ones) to be placed on the <a href="/wiki/Official_Roll_of_the_Baronetage" title="Official Roll of the Baronetage">Roll of Baronets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-whatdotheyknow_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatdotheyknow-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Committee for the Affairs of Jersey and Guernsey recommends approval of <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a> legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-whatdotheyknow_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatdotheyknow-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Committee for the purposes of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Seal_of_the_Realm" title="Great Seal of the Realm">Crown Office Act 1877</a> consists of the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chancellor" title="Lord Chancellor">Lord Chancellor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lord_Privy_Seal" title="Lord Privy Seal">Lord Privy Seal</a> as well as a <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a>. The Committee which last met in 1988 is concerned with the design and usage of <a href="/wiki/Seal_(contract_law)" title="Seal (contract law)">wafer seals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-whatdotheyknow_84-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatdotheyknow-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Scottish Universities Committee considers proposed amendments to the statutes of Scotland\'s four ancient universities.<sup id="cite_ref-whatdotheyknow_84-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatdotheyknow-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>  The Universities Committee, which last met in 1995, considers <a href="/wiki/Petition" title="Petition">petitions</a> against statutes\nmade by Oxford and Cambridge Universities and their colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-whatdotheyknow_84-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatdotheyknow-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council" title="Judicial Committee of the Privy Council">Judicial Committee of the Privy Council</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> consists of senior judges who are Privy Counsellors.<sup id="cite_ref-gay-p6_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p6-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The decision of the Committee is presented in the form of "advice" to the monarch, but in practice it is always followed by the sovereign (as Crown-in-Council), who formally approves the recommendation of the Judicial Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Within the United Kingdom, the Judicial Committee hears appeals from <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_courts" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecclesiastical courts">ecclesiastical courts</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_court" title="Admiralty court">Court of Admiralty</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Cinque_Ports" title="Cinque Ports">Cinque Ports</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prize_court" title="Prize court">prize courts</a> and the Disciplinary Committee of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Veterinary_Surgeons" title="Royal College of Veterinary Surgeons">Royal College of Veterinary Surgeons</a>, appeals against schemes of the <a href="/wiki/Church_Commissioners" title="Church Commissioners">Church Commissioners</a> and appeals under certain Acts of Parliament (e.g., the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_Disqualification_Act_1975" title="House of Commons Disqualification Act 1975">House of Commons Disqualification Act 1975</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-pco-jurisdiction_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pco-jurisdiction-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The Crown-in-Council was formerly the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal" class="mw-redirect" title="Court of Appeal">Supreme Appeal Court</a> for the entire <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> but a number of Commonwealth countries have now abolished the right to such appeals.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The Judicial Committee continues to hear appeals from several Commonwealth countries, from <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_Base_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Sovereign Base Area">Sovereign Base Areas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">Crown dependencies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pco-jurisdiction_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pco-jurisdiction-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>  The Judicial Committee had direct jurisdiction in cases relating to the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Act_1998" title="Scotland Act 1998">Scotland Act 1998</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Wales_Act_1998" title="Government of Wales Act 1998">Government of Wales Act 1998</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Act_1998" title="Northern Ireland Act 1998">Northern Ireland Act 1998</a>, but this was transferred to the new <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Supreme Court of the United Kingdom">Supreme Court of the United Kingdom</a> in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-gay-p6_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gay-p6-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition to the Standing Committees, <i><a href="/wiki/Ad_hoc" title="Ad hoc">ad hoc</a></i> Committees are notionally set up to consider and report on Petitions for <a href="/wiki/Royal_charter" title="Royal charter">Royal Charters of Incorporation</a> and to approve changes to the <a href="/wiki/Bye-law" class="mw-redirect" title="Bye-law">bye-laws</a> of <a href="/wiki/Corporate_body" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate body">bodies</a> created by Royal Charter.<sup id="cite_ref-whatdotheyknow_84-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatdotheyknow-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Committees of Privy Counsellors are occasionally established to examine specific issues. Such Committees are independent of the\nPrivy Council Office and therefore do not report directly to the Lord President of the Council.<sup id="cite_ref-whatdotheyknow_84-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatdotheyknow-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Examples of such Committees include:<sup id="cite_ref-whatdotheyknow_84-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatdotheyknow-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>the <a href="/wiki/Butler_Review" title="Butler Review">Butler Committee</a>\xe2\x80\x94operation of the intelligence services in the runup to military intervention in Iraq</li>\n<li>the Chilcot Committee\xe2\x80\x94for the <a href="/wiki/Chilcot_Inquiry" class="mw-redirect" title="Chilcot Inquiry">Chilcot Inquiry</a> on the use of intercept materials</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Peter_Gibson" title="Peter Gibson">Gibson Committee</a> of enquiry set up in 2010\xe2\x80\x94to consider whether the <a href="/wiki/UK_security_services" class="mw-redirect" title="UK security services">UK security services</a> were complicit in torture of detainees.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_orders">Notable orders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Notable orders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Civil_Service_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Service (United Kingdom)">Civil Service</a> is formally governed by <a href="/wiki/List_of_Privy_Council_Orders" title="List of Privy Council Orders">Privy Council Orders</a>, as an exercise of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_prerogative" title="Royal prerogative">Royal prerogative</a>. One such order implemented HM Government\'s ban of <a href="/wiki/Government_Communications_Headquarters" title="Government Communications Headquarters">GCHQ</a> staff from joining a Trade Union.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Another, the Civil Service (Amendment) Order in Council 1997, permitted the Prime Minister to grant up to three <a href="/wiki/Special_advisers_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Special advisers in the United Kingdom">political advisers</a> management authority over some Civil Servants.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC090512_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC090512-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 1960s, the Privy Council made an order to evict the 2,000 inhabitants of the 65-island <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago" title="Chagos Archipelago">Chagos Archipelago</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>, in preparation for the establishment of a joint United States\xe2\x80\x93United Kingdom military base on the largest outlying island, <a href="/wiki/Diego_Garcia" title="Diego Garcia">Diego Garcia</a>, some 60 miles (97&#160;km) distant. In 2000 the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal_of_England_and_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="Court of Appeal of England and Wales">Court of Appeal</a> ruled the <a href="/wiki/Immigration_Act_1971" title="Immigration Act 1971">1971 Immigration Ordinance</a> preventing resettlement unlawful. In 2004, the Privy Council, under <a href="/wiki/Jack_Straw" title="Jack Straw">Jack Straw</a>\'s tenure, overturned the ruling. In 2006 the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice" title="High Court of Justice">High Court of Justice</a> found the Privy Council\'s decision to be unlawful. <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Kentridge" title="Sydney Kentridge">Sir Sydney Kentridge</a> described the treatment of the <a href="/wiki/Chagossians" title="Chagossians">Chagossians</a> as "outrageous, unlawful and a breach of accepted moral standards": Justice Kentridge stated that there was no known <a href="/wiki/Precedent" title="Precedent">precedent</a> "for the lawful use of prerogative powers to remove or exclude an entire population of British subjects from their homes and place of birth",<sup id="cite_ref-BBC090512_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC090512-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EWCA2007_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EWCA2007-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC060511_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC060511-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> and the Court of Appeal were persuaded by this argument, but the <a href="/wiki/Law_Lords" class="mw-redirect" title="Law Lords">Law Lords</a> (at that time the UK\'s highest <a href="/wiki/Law_court" class="mw-redirect" title="Law court">law court</a>) found its decision to be flawed and overturned the ruling by a 3\xe2\x80\x932 decision thereby upholding the terms of the Ordinance.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rights_and_privileges_of_members">Rights and privileges of members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Rights and privileges of members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Privy Council as a whole is termed "<a href="/wiki/The_Most_Honourable" title="The Most Honourable">The Most Honourable</a>" whilst its members individually, the Privy Counsellors, are entitled to be <a href="/wiki/Style_(manner_of_address)" title="Style (manner of address)">styled</a> "<a href="/wiki/The_Right_Honourable" title="The Right Honourable">The Right Honourable</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Each Privy Counsellor has the right of personal access to the sovereign. Peers were considered to enjoy this right individually; members of the House of Commons possess the right collectively. In each case, personal access may only be used to tender advice on <a href="/wiki/Public_policy" title="Public policy">public affairs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cox-25_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cox-25-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Only Privy Counsellors can signify royal consent to the examination of a <a href="/wiki/Bill_(law)" title="Bill (law)">Bill</a> affecting the rights of the Crown.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Members of the Privy Council are privileged to be given advance notice of any <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">prime ministerial</a> decision to commit <a href="/wiki/HM_Armed_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="HM Armed Forces">HM Armed Forces</a> in <a href="/wiki/Military_operation" title="Military operation">enemy action</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Privy Counsellors have the right to sit on the steps of the Sovereign\'s Throne in the Chamber of the House of Lords during debates, a privilege which was shared with <a href="/wiki/Heirs_apparent" class="mw-redirect" title="Heirs apparent">heirs apparent</a> of those <a href="/wiki/Hereditary_peerage" class="mw-redirect" title="Hereditary peerage">hereditary peers</a> who were to become members of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a> before Labour\'s partial <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords_Act_1999" title="House of Lords Act 1999">Reform of the Lords</a> in 1999, diocesan bishops of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> yet to be <a href="/wiki/Lords_Spiritual" title="Lords Spiritual">Lords Spiritual</a>, retired bishops who formerly sat in the House of Lords, the <a href="/wiki/Dean_of_Westminster" title="Dean of Westminster">Dean of Westminster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peerage_of_Ireland" title="Peerage of Ireland">Peers of Ireland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Clerk_of_the_Crown_in_Chancery" title="Clerk of the Crown in Chancery">Clerk of the Crown in Chancery</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Rod" title="Black Rod">Gentleman Usher of the Black Rod</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> While Privy Counsellors have the right to sit on the steps of the Sovereign\'s Throne they do so only as observers and are not allowed to participate in any of the workings of the House of Lords. Nowadays this privilege is rarely exercised. A notable recent instance of the exercising of this privilege was used by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a>, who watched the opening of the debate of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_(Notification_of_Withdrawal)_Bill_2017" class="mw-redirect" title="European Union (Notification of Withdrawal) Bill 2017">European Union (Notification of Withdrawal) Bill 2017</a> in the House of Lords.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Privy Counsellors are accorded a formal rank of <a href="/wiki/Order_of_precedence_in_England_and_Wales" title="Order of precedence in England and Wales">precedence</a>, if not already having a higher one.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> At the beginning of each new Parliament, and at the discretion of the <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_House_of_Commons_(United_Kingdom)" title="Speaker of the House of Commons (United Kingdom)">Speaker</a>, those members of the House of Commons who are Privy Counsellors usually take the oath of allegiance before all other members except the Speaker and the <a href="/wiki/Father_of_the_House" title="Father of the House">Father of the House</a>, who is the most senior member of the House.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Should a Privy Counsellor rise to speak in the House of Commons at the same time as another <a href="/wiki/Member_of_parliament" title="Member of parliament">Honourable Member</a>, the Speaker usually gives priority to the "Right Honourable" Member.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> This parliamentary custom, however, was discouraged under <a href="/wiki/New_Labour" title="New Labour">New Labour</a> after 1998, despite the Government not being supposed to exert influence over the Speaker.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>All those sworn of the Privy Council below the rank of <a href="/wiki/Marquess" title="Marquess">marquess</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Baron" title="Baron">barons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viscount" title="Viscount">viscounts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Earl" title="Earl">earls</a>, are accorded the style "The Right Honourable"; privy counsellor <a href="/wiki/Duke" title="Duke">non-royal dukes</a> are styled "<a href="/wiki/The_Most_Noble" title="The Most Noble">The Most Noble</a>" and marquesses, "The Most Honourable".  Modern custom as recommended by <i><a href="/wiki/Debrett%27s" title="Debrett&#39;s">Debrett\'s</a></i> is to use the post-nominal letters "PC" in a social style of address for <a href="/wiki/Peerage" title="Peerage">peers</a> who are Privy Counsellors.<sup id="cite_ref-DebrettPC_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DebrettPC-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> For <a href="/wiki/Commoner" title="Commoner">commoners</a>, "The Right Honourable" is sufficient identification of their status as a Privy Counsellor and they do not use the post-nominal letters "PC".<sup id="cite_ref-nz-pc_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nz-pc-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DebrettPC_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DebrettPC-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Justice" title="Ministry of Justice">Ministry of Justice</a> revises current practice of this convention from time to time.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_councils">Other councils</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Other councils">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Privy Council is one of the four principal councils of the sovereign. The other three are the courts of law, the <i><a href="/wiki/Commune_Concilium" class="mw-redirect" title="Commune Concilium">Commune Concilium</a></i> (Common Council, or Parliament) and the <i><a href="/wiki/Magnum_Concilium" title="Magnum Concilium">Magnum Concilium</a></i> (Great Council, or the assembly of all the <a href="/wiki/Peers_of_the_Realm" class="mw-redirect" title="Peers of the Realm">Peers of the Realm</a>). All are still in existence, or at least have never been formally abolished, but the <i>Magnum Concilium</i> has not been summoned since 1640 and was considered defunct even then.<sup id="cite_ref-cox-25_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cox-25-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Several other Privy Councils have advised the sovereign. England and Scotland once had separate Privy Councils (the <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_England" title="Privy Council of England">Privy Council of England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_Scotland" title="Privy Council of Scotland">Privy Council of Scotland</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Acts of Union 1707</a> united the two countries into the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a> and in 1708 the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Great_Britain" title="Parliament of Great Britain">Parliament of Great Britain</a> abolished the Privy Council of Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Thereafter there was one Privy Council of Great Britain sitting in London.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ireland" title="Kingdom of Ireland">Ireland</a>, on the other hand, continued to have a separate Privy Council even after the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Union_1800" class="mw-redirect" title="Act of Union 1800">Act of Union 1800</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_Ireland" title="Privy Council of Ireland">Privy Council of Ireland</a> was abolished in 1922, when <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ireland_(1921%E2%80%9322)" title="Southern Ireland (1921\xe2\x80\x9322)">the southern part of Ireland</a> separated from the United Kingdom; it was succeeded by the <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Privy Council of Northern Ireland">Privy Council of Northern Ireland</a>, which became dormant after the suspension of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Parliament of Northern Ireland">Parliament of Northern Ireland</a> in 1972. No further appointments have been made since then, and only three appointees were still living as of November 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> has had its own Privy Council\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Privy_Council_for_Canada" title="Queen&#39;s Privy Council for Canada">Queen\'s Privy Council for Canada</a>\xe2\x80\x94since 1867.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> While the Canadian Privy Council is specifically "for Canada", the Privy Council discussed above is not "for the United Kingdom"; in order to clarify the ambiguity where necessary, the latter was traditionally referred to as the Imperial Privy Council. Equivalent organs of state in other Commonwealth realms, such as Australia and New Zealand, are called <a href="/wiki/Executive_Council_(Commonwealth_countries)" title="Executive Council (Commonwealth countries)">Executive Councils</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Royal_members_of_the_Privy_Council" title="List of Royal members of the Privy Council">List of Royal members of the Privy Council</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_current_members_of_the_British_Privy_Council" title="List of current members of the British Privy Council">List of current Privy Counsellors</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_longest-serving_current_Privy_Counsellors" title="List of longest-serving current Privy Counsellors">List of longest-serving current Privy Counsellors</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_senior_members_of_the_Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of senior members of the Privy Council of the United Kingdom">List of senior members of the Privy Council of the United Kingdom</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Privy_Council_Orders" title="List of Privy Council Orders">List of Privy Council Orders</a></li>\n<li><a &amp; Baronetage</i></a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
