Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2016-10-12</span></span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Guardian&amp;rft.atitle=Jeremy+Corbyn+rejects+formal+privy+council+induction+by+Queen&amp;rft.date=2015-10-08&amp;rft.issn=0261-3077&amp;rft.aulast=Wintour&amp;rft.aufirst=Patrick&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.theguardian.com%2Flaw%2F2015%2Foct%2F08%2Fjeremy-corbyn-rejects-formal-privy-council-induction-by-queen&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APrivy+Council+of+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-46">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Blackstone, I. 176.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-47"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-47">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The most recent enactment deferring dissolution was the Succession to the Crown Act 1707 (6 <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Queen_of_Great_Britain" title="Anne, Queen of Great Britain">Ann.</a> c. 41). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jacobite.ca/documents/1707security.htm">Complete text</a> as originally enacted. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.legislation.gov.uk/apgb/Ann/6/41/contents">Text of the Succession to the Crown Act 1707</a> as in force today (including any amendments) within the United Kingdom, from <a href="/wiki/Legislation.gov.uk" title="Legislation.gov.uk">legislation.gov.uk</a> . Section VIII provided, "... the Privy Council of Her Majesty, her heirs or successors for the Kingdom of Great Britain, shall not be determined or dissolved by the death or demise of Her Majesty, her heirs or successors; but such Privy Council shall continue and act as such by the space of six months next after such demise, unless sooner determined by the next successor to whom the imperial Crown of this realm is limited and appointed to go, remain, and descend; ..." Despite becoming obsolete in 1901, this section remained on the statute book until it was repealed by the Statute Law (Repeals) Act 1973 (c. 39), section 1(1) and Schedule 1 part I.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-48"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-48">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">H.&#160;Cox, p. 389.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-49">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See, for example, the proclamation following the accession of <a href="/wiki/Victoria_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria of the United Kingdom">Queen Victoria</a> on the death of <a href="/wiki/William_IV_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="William IV of the United Kingdom">William IV</a>: <cite class="citation journal"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.london-gazette.co.uk/issues/19514/pages/1625">"By the Queen: A Proclamation: Requiring all Persons, being in Office of Authority or Government at the Decease of the late King, to proceed in the Execution of their respective Offices"</a>. <i>The London Gazette</i>. London: Francis Watts (19514): 1625\xe2\x80\x931626. 27 June 1837<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">7 June</span> 2010</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+London+Gazette&amp;rft.atitle=By+the+Queen%3A+A+Proclamation%3A+Requiring+all+Persons%2C+being+in+Office+of+Authority+or+Government+at+the+Decease+of+the+late+King%2C+to+proceed+in+the+Execution+of+their+respective+Offices&amp;rft.issue=19514&amp;rft.pages=1625-1626&amp;rft.date=1837-06-27&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.london-gazette.co.uk%2Fissues%2F19514%2Fpages%2F1625&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APrivy+Council+of+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Demise of the Crown Act 1901 (1 <a href="/wiki/Edward_VII_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward VII of the United Kingdom">Edw. 7</a> c. 5), <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.opsi.gov.uk/acts/acts1901/pdf/ukpga_19010005_en.pdf">"An Act to amend the Law relating to the Holding of Offices in case of the Demise of the Crown"</a> (original text), <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.legislation.gov.uk/id?title=Demise+of+the+Crown+Act+1901">Text of the Demise of the Crown Act 1901</a> as in force today (including any amendments) within the United Kingdom, from <a href="/wiki/Legislation.gov.uk" title="Legislation.gov.uk">legislation.gov.uk</a> . Section 1(1) provides, "The holding of any office under the Crown, whether within or without His Majesty\'s dominions, shall not be affected, nor shall any fresh appointment thereto be rendered necessary, by the demise of the Crown." The act came into force within six months of the death of Victoria and section 1(2) ensured that no offices were vacated on the subsequent accession of Edward VII. See also commentary in Appendix 2 of the report that preceded the 1973 Act: <cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/Law_Commission_(England_and_Wales)" title="Law Commission (England and Wales)">Law Commission</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Law_Commission" title="Scottish Law Commission">Scottish Law Commission</a> (1972). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.scotlawcom.gov.uk/download_file/view/284/"><i>Statute Law Revision: Fourth Report</i></a>. London: <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Stationery_Office" class="mw-redirect" title="Her Majesty&#39;s Stationery Office">Her Majesty\'s Stationery Office</a>. pp.&#160;30\xe2\x80\x9355. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-10-151080-2" title="Special:BookSources/0-10-151080-2">0-10-151080-2</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">7 June</span> 2010</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Statute+Law+Revision%3A+Fourth+Report&amp;rft.place=London&amp;rft.pages=30-55&amp;rft.pub=Her+Majesty%27s+Stationery+Office&amp;rft.date=1972&amp;rft.isbn=0-10-151080-2&amp;rft.au=Law+Commission%2C+Scottish+Law+Commission&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.scotlawcom.gov.uk%2Fdownload_file%2Fview%2F284%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APrivy+Council+of+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> (LC 49, SLC 26, Cmnd 5108).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text"
